<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">ExxonMobil</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>

<p><b>Exxon Mobil Corporation</b>,  <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">doing business as</a> <b>ExxonMobil</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_exploration_and_production_companies" title="List of oil exploration and production companies">oil and gas</a> corporation headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>. It is the largest direct descendant of <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Company" title="Standard Oil Company">Standard Oil Company</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exxonmobilhistory_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilhistory-2">[2]</a></sup> and was formed on November 30, 1999 by the merger of <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a> (formerly the Standard Oil Company of New Jersey) and <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a> (formerly the Standard Oil Company of New York).
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_companies_by_revenue" title="List of companies by revenue">world's 10th largest company by revenue</a>, ExxonMobil from 1996 to 2017 varied from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_by_market_capitalization" title="List of corporations by market capitalization">first to sixth largest publicly traded company by market capitalization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes2000_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2000-4">[4]</a></sup> The company was ranked ninth globally in the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a> list in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> ExxonMobil was the second most profitable company in the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>ExxonMobil is the largest of the world's <a href="/wiki/Big_Oil" title="Big Oil">Big Oil</a> companies, or supermajors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> with daily production of 3.921 million BOE (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrels_of_oil_equivalent" title="Barrels of oil equivalent">barrels of oil equivalent</a>); but significantly smaller than a number of national companies. In 2008, this was approximately 3 percent of world production, which is less than several of the largest state-owned petroleum companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> When ranked by oil and gas reserves, it is 14th in the world—with less than 1 percent of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> ExxonMobil's reserves were 20 billion BOE at the end of 2016 and the 2007 rates of production were expected to last more than 14 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> With 37 <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a> in 21 countries constituting a combined daily refining capacity of 6.3 million barrels (1,000,000 m<sup>3</sup>), ExxonMobil is the largest refiner in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> a title that was also associated with Standard Oil since its incorporation in 1870.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exxonmobilhistory_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-exxonmobilhistory-2">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>ExxonMobil has been criticized for its slow response to cleanup efforts after the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> in Alaska, widely considered to be one of the world's worst oil spills in terms of damage to the environment. ExxonMobil has a history of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels_lobby" title="Fossil fuels lobby">lobbying</a> for <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a> and against the scientific consensus that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> is caused by the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>. The company has also been the target of accusations of improperly dealing with human rights issues, influence on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_foreign_policy" title="American foreign policy">American foreign policy</a>, and its impact on the future of nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tel12_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="750" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/220px-Big_Oil.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/330px-Big_Oil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/440px-Big_Oil.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chart of the major energy companies dubbed "Big Oil", sorted by latest published revenue</div></div></div>
<p>ExxonMobil was formed in 1999 by the merger of two major oil companies, Exxon and Mobil.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1870_to_1911">1870 to 1911</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1870 to 1911">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a></div>
<p>Both Exxon and Mobil were descendants of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a>, established by <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a> and partners in 1870 as the Standard Oil Company of Ohio. In 1882, it together with its affiliated companies was incorporated as the Standard Oil Trust with Standard Oil Company of New Jersey and Standard Oil Company of New York as its largest companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-American_Oil_Company" title="Anglo-American Oil Company">Anglo-American Oil Company</a> was established in the United Kingdom in 1888.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grace_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-grace-17">[17]</a></sup>  In 1890, Standard Oil, together with local ship merchants in Bremen established <i>Deutsch-Amerikanische Petroleum Gesellschaft</i> (later: Esso A.G.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clark_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-clark-19">[19]</a></sup>  In 1891, a sale branch for the Netherlands and Belgium, American Petroleum Company, was established in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-krabbendam_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-krabbendam-20">[20]</a></sup>  At the same year, a sale branch for Italy, <i>Società Italo Americana pel Petrolio</i>, was established in <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skinner_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-skinner-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Standard Oil Trust was dissolved under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a> in 1892; however, it reemerged as the Standard Oil Interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>  In 1893, the Chinese and the whole Asian <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> market was assigned to Standard Oil Company of New York in order to improve trade with the Asian counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cochran_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-cochran-22">[22]</a></sup>  In 1898, Standard Oil of New Jersey acquired controlling stake in <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Oil" title="Imperial Oil">Imperial Oil</a> of Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-18">[18]</a></sup>  In 1899, Standard Oil Company of New Jersey became the holding company for the Standard Oil Interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>  The anti-monopoly proceedings against the Standard Oil were launched in 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>  The reputation of Standard Oil in the public eye suffered badly after publication of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ida_M._Tarbell" title="Ida M. Tarbell">Ida M. Tarbell</a>'s classic exposé <i><a href="/wiki/The_History_of_the_Standard_Oil_Company" title="The History of the Standard Oil Company">The History of the Standard Oil Co.</a></i> in 1904, leading to a growing outcry for the government to take action against the company. By 1911, with <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">public outcry</a> at a climax, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Company_of_New_Jersey_v._United_States" title="Standard Oil Company of New Jersey v. United States">ruled</a> that Standard Oil must be dissolved and split into 34 companies. Two of these companies were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_New_Jersey" title="Standard Oil of New Jersey">Jersey Standard</a> ("Standard Oil Co. of New Jersey"), which eventually became Exxon, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socony" title="Socony">Socony</a> ("Standard Oil Co. of New York"), which eventually became Mobil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1911_to_1950">1911 to 1950</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1911 to 1950">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Over the next few decades, Jersey Standard and Socony grew significantly. John Duston Archbold was the first president of Jersey Standard. Archbold was followed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_C._Teagle" title="Walter C. Teagle">Walter C. Teagle</a> in 1917, who made it the largest oil company in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>  In 1919, Jersey Standard acquired a 50% share in <a href="/wiki/Humble_Oil" title="Humble Oil">Humble Oil &amp; Refining Co.</a>, a Texas oil producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>  In 1920, it was listed on the New York Stock Exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup> In the following years it acquired or established Tropical Oil Company of Colombia (1920), Standard Oil Company of Venezuela (1921), and Creole Petroleum Company of Venezuela (1928).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-exxon_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-exxon-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay_Folger" title="Henry Clay Folger">Henry Clay Folger</a> was head of Socony until 1923, when he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_L._Pratt" title="Herbert L. Pratt">Herbert L. Pratt</a>. The growing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">automotive</a> market inspired the product trademark Mobiloil, registered by Socony in 1920.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  After dissolution of Standard Oil, Socony had refining and marketing assets but no production activities. For this reason, Socony purchased a 45% interest in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnolia_Petroleum_Co." title="Magnolia Petroleum Co.">Magnolia Petroleum Co.</a>, a major refiner, marketer and pipeline transporter, in 1918. In 1925, Magnolia became wholly owned by Socony. In 1926, Socony purchased General Petroleum Corporation of California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>  In 1928, Socony joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Petroleum_Company" title="Turkish Petroleum Company">Turkish Petroleum Company</a> (Iraq Petroleum Company).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>  In 1931, Socony merged with <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_Oil_Company" title="Vacuum Oil Company">Vacuum Oil Company</a>, an industry pioneer dating back to 1866, to form Socony-Vacuum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time100831_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-time100831-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Asia-Pacific region, Jersey Standard has established through its Dutch subsidiary an exploration and production company <i>Nederlandsche Koloniale Petroleum Maatschappij</i> in 1912. In 1922, it found oil in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and in 1927, it built a refinery in <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shavit_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-shavit-25">[25]</a></sup>  It had oil production and refineries but no marketing network. Socony-Vacuum had Asian marketing outlets supplied remotely from California. In 1933, Jersey Standard and Socony-Vacuum merged their interests in the Asia-Pacific region into a 50–50 joint venture. <a href="/wiki/Standard_Vacuum_Oil_Company" title="Standard Vacuum Oil Company">Standard Vacuum Oil Company</a>, or "Stanvac," operated in 50 countries, from East Africa to New Zealand, before it was dissolved in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924, Jersey Standard and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> pooled its <a href="/wiki/Tetraethyllead" title="Tetraethyllead">tetraethyllead</a>-related patents and established the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethyl_Gasoline_Corporation" title="Ethyl Gasoline Corporation">Ethyl Gasoline Corporation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pound_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-pound-26">[26]</a></sup>  In 1927, Jersey Standard signed a 25-years cooperation agreement with <a href="/wiki/IG_Farben" title="IG Farben">IG Farben</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_hydrogenation" title="Coal hydrogenation">coal hydrogenation</a> research in the United States.  Jersey Standard assumed this cooperation to be beneficial as it believed the United States oil reserves to be exhausted in the near future and that the coal hydrogenation would give an access for producing <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_fuel" title="Synthetic fuel">synthetic fuels</a>. It erected synthetic fuel plants in <a href="/wiki/Bayway_Refinery" title="Bayway Refinery">Bayway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge_Refinery" title="Baton Rouge Refinery">Baton Rouge</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baytown_Refinery" title="Baytown Refinery">Baytown</a> (unfinished). The interest in hydrogenation evaporated after discovery of the <a href="/wiki/East_Texas_Oil_Field" title="East Texas Oil Field">East Texas Oil Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lesch_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-lesch-27">[27]</a></sup>  As a part of the cooperation between Jersey Standard and IG Farben, a joint company, Standard I.G. Company, was established with Jersey Standard having a stake of 80%.  IG Farben transferred rights to the hydrogenation process outside of Germany to the joint venture in exchange of $35 million stake of Jersey Standard shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herbert_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-herbert-28">[28]</a></sup>  In 1930, the joint company established Hydro Patents Company to license the hydrogenation process in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nowell_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-nowell-29">[29]</a></sup>  The agreement with IG Farben gave to Jersey Standard access to patents related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polyisobutylene" title="Polyisobutylene">polyisobutylene</a> which assist Jersey Standard to advance in isobutolene polymerization and to produce the first <a href="/wiki/Butyl_rubber" title="Butyl rubber">butyl rubber</a> in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-butyl_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-butyl-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-morton-31">[31]</a></sup>  As the agreement with IG Farben gave to the German company a veto right of licensing chemical industry patents in the United States, including patent for butyl rubber, Jersey Standard was accused of treason by senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rockoff_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-rockoff-32">[32]</a></sup>  In 1941, it opened the first commercial synthetic <a href="/wiki/Toluene" title="Toluene">toluene</a> plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1932, Jersey Standard acquired foreign assets of the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Petroleum_and_Transport_Company" title="Pan American Petroleum and Transport Company">Pan American Petroleum and Transport Company</a>. In 1937, its assets in Bolivia were nationalized, followed by nationalization of its assets in Mexico in 1938.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1935, Socony Vacuum Oil opened the huge Mammoth Oil Port on <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a> which had a capacity of handling a quarter of a billion gallons of petroleum products a year and could transship oil from ocean-going tankers and river barges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popular_Mechanics_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Popular_Mechanics-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1940, Socony-Vacuum purchased the Gilmore Oil Company of California, which 1946 was merged with its another subsidiary, General Petroleum Corporation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darr_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-darr-34">[34]</a></sup>  In 1947, Jersey Standard and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> formed a joint venture <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nederlandse_Aardolie_Maatschappij_BV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij BV (page does not exist)">Nederlandse Aardolie Maatschappij BV</a> for oil and gas exploration and production in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tjemkes_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-tjemkes-35">[35]</a></sup>  In 1948, Jersey Standard and Socony-Vacuum acquired interests in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab-American_Oil_Company" title="Arab-American Oil Company">Arab-American Oil Company</a> (Aramco).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-green_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-green-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950_to_1972">1950 to 1972</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1950 to 1972">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1955, Socony-Vacuum became Socony Mobil Oil Company.  In 1959, Magnolia Petroleum Company, General Petroleum Corporation, and Mobil Producing Company were merged to form the Mobil Oil Company, a <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">wholly owned subsidiary</a> of Socony Mobil. In 1966, Socony Mobil Oil Company became the Mobil Oil Corporation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-9"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Humble Oil became a wholly owned subsidiary of Jersey Standard and was reorganized into the United States marketing division of Jersey Standard in 1959.  In 1967, Humble Oil purchased all remaining Signal stations from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Company_of_California" title="Standard Oil Company of California">Standard Oil Company of California</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>) In 1969, Humble Oil opened a new refinery in <a href="/wiki/Benicia,_California" title="Benicia, California">Benicia, California</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In Libya, Jersey Standard made its first major oil discovery in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-10"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mobil Chemical Company was established in 1960 and Exxon Chemical Company (first named Enjay Chemicals) in 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-11"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1965, Jersey Standard started to acquire coal assets through its affiliate Carter Oil (later renamed: Exxon Coal, U.S.A.). For managing the Midwest and Eastern coal assets in the United States, the Monterey Coal Company was established in 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chakravarthy_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-chakravarthy-37">[37]</a></sup>  Carter Oil focused on the developing synthetic fuels from coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chakravarthy_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-chakravarthy-37">[37]</a></sup> In 1966, it started to develop the <a href="/wiki/Coal_liquefaction" title="Coal liquefaction">coal liquefaction</a> process called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exxon_Donor_Solvent_Process" title="Exxon Donor Solvent Process">Exxon Donor Solvent Process</a>. In April 1980, Exxon opened a 250-ton-per-day pilot plant in <a href="/wiki/Baytown,_Texas" title="Baytown, Texas">Baytown, Texas</a>. The plant was closed and dismantled in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kent_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-kent-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1967, Mobil acquired a 28% strategic stake in the German fuel chain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aral_A.G." title="Aral A.G.">Aral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weiand_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 1960s Jersey Standard task force was looking for projects 30 years in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-williams_2005_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-williams_2005-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perlin_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-perlin-41">[41]</a></sup> In April 1973, Exxon founded Solar Power Corporation, a wholly owned subsidiary for manufacturing of terrestrial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_cell" title="Photovoltaic cell">photovoltaic cells</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jones_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-jones-42">[42]</a></sup>  After <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1980s oil glut</a> Exxon's internal report projected that solar would not become viable until 2012 or 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg041115_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg041115-43">[43]</a></sup>  Consequently, Exxon sold Solar Power Corporation in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jones_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-jones-42">[42]</a></sup>  In 1974–1994, also Mobil developed solar energy through Mobil Tyco Solar Energy Corporation, its joint venture with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tyco_Laboratories" title="Tyco Laboratories">Tyco Laboratories</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jones_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-jones-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muhlbauer_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-muhlbauer-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 1960s, Jersey Standard entered into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_industry" title="Nuclear industry">nuclear industry</a>. In 1969, it created a subsidiary, Jersey Nuclear Company (later: Exxon Nuclear Company), for manufacturing and marketing of uranium fuel, which was to be fabricated from uranium concentrates mined by the mineral department of Humble Oil (later: Exxon Minerals Company).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taylor220883_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-taylor220883-45">[45]</a></sup>  In 1970, Jersey Nuclear opened a nuclear fuel manufacturing facility, now owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Areva" title="Areva">Areva</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Richland,_Washington" title="Richland, Washington">Richland, Washington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-areva301015_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-areva301015-46">[46]</a></sup>  In 1986, Exxon Nuclear was sold to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kraftwerk_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kraftwerk Union (page does not exist)">Kraftwerk Union</a>, a nuclear arm of <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ferguson_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ferguson-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt241286_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt241286-48">[48]</a></sup> The company started surface mining of uranium ore in <a href="/wiki/Converse_County,_Wyoming" title="Converse County, Wyoming">Converse County, Wyoming</a>, in 1970, solution mining in 1972, and underground mining in 1977. Uranium ore processing started in 1972. The facility was closed in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc-highlands_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrc-highlands-49">[49]</a></sup>  In 1973, Exxon acquired the <a href="/wiki/Ray_Point,_Texas" title="Ray Point, Texas">Ray Point</a> uranium ore processing facility which was shortly afterwards decommissioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc-texas_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrc-texas-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1972_to_1998">1972 to 1998</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1972 to 1998">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1972, Exxon was unveiled as the new, unified brand name for all former Enco and Esso outlets. At the same time, the company changed its corporate name from Standard Oil of New Jersey to Exxon Corporation, and Humble Oil became Exxon Company, U.S.A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-12"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>  The rebranding came after successful test-marketing of the Exxon name, under two experimental logos, in the fall and winter of 1971-72. Along with the new name, Exxon settled on a rectangular logo using red lettering and blue trim on a white background, similar to the familiar color scheme on the old Enco and Esso logos. Exxon replaced the <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enco_(oil_company)" title="Enco (oil company)">Enco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Humble_Oil" title="Humble Oil">Humble</a> brands in the United States on January 1, 1973.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">oil embargo of 1973</a>, Exxon and Mobil began to expand their exploration and production into the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, Africa and Asia. Mobil diversified its activities into retail sale by acquiring the parent company of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montgomery_Ward_and_Container_Corporation" title="Montgomery Ward and Container Corporation">Montgomery Ward and Container Corporation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historical_Note_16-13"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1976, Exxon, through its subsidiary Intercor, entered into partnership with Colombian state owned company Carbocol to start coal mining in <a href="/wiki/Cerrej%C3%B3n" title="Cerrejón">Cerrejón</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cerrejon_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-cerrejon-51">[51]</a></sup>  In 1980, Exxon merged its assets in the mineral industry into newly established Exxon Minerals (later ExxonMobil Coal and Minerals).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obrien_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-obrien-52">[52]</a></sup>  At the same year, Exxon entered into the <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_industry" title="Oil shale industry">oil shale industry</a> by buying a 60% stake in the <a href="/wiki/Colony_Shale_Oil_Project" title="Colony Shale Oil Project">Colony Shale Oil Project</a> in Colorado, United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fu_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-fu-53">[53]</a></sup> and 50% stake in the Rundle oil shale deposit in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-symington_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-symington-54">[54]</a></sup>  On May 2, 1982, Exxon announced the termination of the Colony Shale Oil Project because of low oil-prices and increased expenses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vassiliou_23-9"><a href="#cite_note-vassiliou-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fu_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-fu-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mobil moved its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> to <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">Fairfax County, Virginia</a>, in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DawsonExxon2_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-DawsonExxon2-55">[55]</a></sup>  Exxon sold the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exxon_Building_(New_York)" title="Exxon Building (New York)">Exxon Building</a> (1251 Avenue of the Americas), its former headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>, to a unit of Mitsui Real Estate Development Co. Ltd. in 1986 for $610 million, and in 1989, moved its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, New York City to the <a href="/wiki/Las_Colinas" title="Las Colinas">Las Colinas</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>. John Walsh, president of Exxon subsidiary Friendswood Development Company, stated that Exxon left New York because the costs were too high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 24, 1989, the <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez" title="Exxon Valdez">Exxon Valdez</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">oil tanker</a> struck <a href="/wiki/Bligh_Reef" title="Bligh Reef">Bligh Reef</a> in <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and spilled more than 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of crude oil. The <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> was the second largest in U.S. history, and in the aftermath of the Exxon Valdez incident, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" title="Congress of the United States">U.S. Congress</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Oil_Pollution_Act_of_1990" title="Oil Pollution Act of 1990">Oil Pollution Act of 1990</a>. An initial award of $5 billion USD <a href="/wiki/Punitive_damages" title="Punitive damages">punitive</a> was reduced to $507.5 million by the US Supreme Court in June 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and distributions of this award have commenced.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 1994, Mobil established a subsidiary MEGAS (Mobil European Gas) which became responsible for its Mobil's natural gas operations in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vap101194_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-vap101194-58">[58]</a></sup>  In 1996, Mobil and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" title="British Petroleum">British Petroleum</a> merged their European refining and marketing of fuels and lubricants businesses.  Mobil had 30% stake in fuels and 51% stake in lubricants businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec070896_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ec070896-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1996, Exxon entered into the Russian market by signing a production sharing agreement on the <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt110696_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt110696-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998_to_2000">1998 to 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1998 to 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, Exxon and Mobil signed a US$73.7 billion merger agreement forming a new company called Exxon Mobil Corp. (ExxonMobil), the largest oil company and the third largest company in the world. This was the largest corporate merger that time. At the time of the merge, Exxon was the world's largest energy company while Mobil was the second largest oil and gas company in the United States. The merger announcement followed shortly after merger of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Petroleum" title="British Petroleum">British Petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> which was the largest industrial merger that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc021298_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc021298-61">[61]</a></sup>  Formally, Mobil was bought by Exxon. Mobil's shareholders received 1.32 Exxon's share for each Mobil's share. As a result, the former Mobil's shareholders receives about 30% in the merged company while the stake of former Exxon's shareholders was about 70%. The head of Exxon <a href="/wiki/Lee_Raymond" title="Lee Raymond">Lee Raymond</a> remained the chairman and chief executive of the new company and Mobil chief executive Lucio Noto became vice-chairman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc021298_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc021298-61">[61]</a></sup>  The merger of Exxon and Mobil was unique in <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">American history</a> because it reunited the two largest companies of Standard Oil trust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt031298_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt031298-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>The merger was approved by the European Commission on September 29, 1999, and by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Federal_Trade_Commission" title="United States Federal Trade Commission">United States Federal Trade Commission</a> on November 30, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec290999_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ec290999-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj011299_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj011299-64">[64]</a></sup>   As a condition for the Exxon and Mobil merger, the European Commission ordered to dissolve the Mobil's partnership with BP, as also to sell its stake in Aral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weiand_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-39">[39]</a></sup>  As a result, BP acquired all fuels assets, two <a href="/wiki/Base_oil" title="Base oil">base oil</a> plants, and a substantial part of the joint venture's finished lubricants business, while ExxonMobil acquired other base oil plants and a part of the finished lubricants business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec030200_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-ec030200-65">[65]</a></sup>  The stake in Aral was sold to Vega Oel, later acquired by BP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weiand_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-weiand-39">[39]</a></sup>  The European Commission also demanded divesting of Mobil's MEGAS and Exxon's 25% stake in the German gas transmission company Thyssengas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ogj251099_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-ogj251099-66">[66]</a></sup>  MEGAS was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Duke_Energy" title="Duke Energy">Duke Energy</a> and the stake in Thyssengas was acquired by RWE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbj030400_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-dbj030400-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbj030400_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-dbj030400-67">[67]</a></sup> The company also divested Exxon's aviation fuel business to BP and Mobil's certain pipeline capacity servicing <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rudnick_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-rudnick-68">[68]</a></sup>  The Federal Trade Commission required to sell 2,431 gas stations in the Northeast and Mid-Atlantic (1,740), California (360), Texas (319), and <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> (12).  In addition, ExxonMobil should sell its <a href="/wiki/Benicia_Refinery" title="Benicia Refinery">Benicia Refinery</a> in California, terminal operations in Boston, the Washington, D.C. area and Guam, interest in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_pipeline" title="Colonial pipeline">Colonial pipeline</a>, Mobil's interest in the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Alaska_Pipeline_System" title="Trans-Alaska Pipeline System">Trans-Alaska Pipeline System</a>, Exxon's jet turbine oil business, and give-up the option to buy <a href="/wiki/Tosco_Corporation" title="Tosco Corporation">Tosco Corporation</a> gas stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn301199_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn301199-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftc301199_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-ftc301199-70">[70]</a></sup>  The Benicia Refinery and 340 Exxon-branded stations in California were bought by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valero_Energy_Corporation" title="Valero Energy Corporation">Valero Energy Corporation</a> in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ogj130300_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-ogj130300-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_to_present">2000 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3328" data-file-width="4992" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg/220px-Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg/330px-Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg/440px-Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vice_President_Cheney_Talks_with_Rex_Tillerson_of_Exxon_Mobil_Corporation_in_His_West_Wing_Office.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ExxonMobil Chairman <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a> with Vice President <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a>, 2007</div></div></div>
<p>In 2002, the company sold its stake in the <a href="/wiki/Cerrej%C3%B3n" title="Cerrejón">Cerrejón</a> coal mine in Colombia, and copper-mining business in Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cerrejon_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-cerrejon-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj030502_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj030502-72">[72]</a></sup>  At the same time, it renewed its interest in oil shale by developing the <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_Electrofrac" title="ExxonMobil Electrofrac">ExxonMobil Electrofrac</a> <i>in-situ</i> extraction process. In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a> approved their research and development project in <a href="/wiki/Rio_Blanco_County,_Colorado" title="Rio Blanco County, Colorado">Rio Blanco County, Colorado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sentinel110314_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-sentinel110314-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oilprice180314_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-oilprice180314-74">[74]</a></sup>  However, in November 2015 the company relinquished its federal research, development and demonstration lease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gjsentinel270316_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-gjsentinel270316-75">[75]</a></sup>  In 2009, ExxonMobil phased-out coal mining by selling its last operational coal mine in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srj270109_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-srj270109-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, ExxonMobil started to phase-out from the United States direct-served retail market by selling its <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">service stations</a>. The usage of Exxon and Mobil brands was <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a> to the new owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erman_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Erman-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, ExxonMobil bought <a href="/wiki/XTO_Energy" title="XTO Energy">XTO Energy</a>, the company focused on development and production of unconventional resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upstream2_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-upstream2-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, ExxonMobil started a strategic cooperation with Russian oil company <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a> to develop the <a href="/wiki/East-Prinovozemelsky_field" title="East-Prinovozemelsky field">East-Prinovozemelsky field</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tuapse_field" title="Tuapse field">Tuapse field</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>  In 2012, ExxonMobil concluded an agreement with Rosneft to assess possibilities to produce <a href="/wiki/Tight_oil" title="Tight oil">tight oil</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bazhenov_Formation" title="Bazhenov Formation">Bazhenov</a> and Achimov formations in <a href="/wiki/Western_Siberia" title="Western Siberia">Western Siberia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj150612_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj150612-80">[80]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In 2018, due to <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">international sanctions imposed against Russia and Rosneft</a>, ExxonMobil announces that it will end ethese joint ventures with Rosneft, but will continue the Sakhalin-I project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The company estimates it would cost about $200 million after tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft010318_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-ft010318-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters280218_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters280218-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, ExxonMobil started a <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane" title="Coalbed methane">coalbed methane</a> development in Australia, but withdrew from the project in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australian171214_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-australian171214-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, ExxonMobil confirmed a deal for production and exploration activities in the Kurdistan region of Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2013, ExxonMobil agreed to sell its majority stakes in a <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>-based utility and power storage firm, Castle Peak Co Ltd, for a total of $3.4 billion, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CLP_Holdings" title="CLP Holdings">CLP Holdings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, ExxonMobil had two "non-monetary" asset swap deals with LINN Energy LLC. In these transactions, ExxonMobil gave to LINN interests in the <a href="/wiki/South_Belridge_Oil_Field" title="South Belridge Oil Field">South Belridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugoton_Gas_Field" title="Hugoton Gas Field">Hugoton</a> gas fields in the exchange of assets in the <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a> in Texas and the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Basin" title="Delaware Basin">Delaware Basin</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ogj190914_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-ogj190914-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 9, 2014, the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Settlement_of_Investment_Disputes" title="International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes">International Centre for Settlement of Investment Disputes</a> awarded ExxonMobil $1.6 billion in the case the company had brought against the Venezuelan government. ExxonMobil alleged that the Venezuelan government illegally expropriated its Venezuelan assets in 2007 and paid unfair compensation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2016, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> contacted ExxonMobil, questioning why (unlike some other companies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>) they had not yet started  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Write-down" title="Write-down">writing down</a> the value of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_reserve" title="Oil reserve">oil reserves</a>, given that much may have to remain in the ground to comply with future climate change legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Carney" title="Mark Carney">Mark Carney</a> has expressed concerns about the industry's "<a href="/wiki/Stranded_asset" title="Stranded asset">stranded assets</a>". In October 2016, ExxonMobil conceded it may need to declare a lower value for its in-ground oil, and that it might write down about one-fifth of its reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 13, 2016, the CEO of ExxonMobil, <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a>, was nominated as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> by <a href="/wiki/President-elect_of_the_United_States" title="President-elect of the United States">President-elect</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2017, Federal climate investigations of ExxonMobil were considered less likely under the new <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 9, 2017, it was revealed that <a href="/wiki/Infineum" title="Infineum">Infineum</a>, a joint venture of ExxonMobil and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a> headquartered in England, conducted business with Iran, Syria, and Sudan while those states were under US sanctions. ExxonMobil representatives said that because Infineum was based in Europe and the transactions did not involve any U.S. employees, this did not violate the sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exxoniran_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-exxoniran-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s administration denied a request from ExxonMobil to allow it to resume <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Russia" title="Petroleum industry in Russia">oil drilling in Russia</a>. Representative <a href="/wiki/Adam_Schiff" title="Adam Schiff">Adam Schiff</a> (D-California) said that the "Treasury Department should reject any waiver from sanctions which would allow Exxon Mobile or any other company to resume business with prohibited Russian entities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, ExxonMobil filed a lawsuit against the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Donald_Trump" title="Cabinet of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a> challenging the finding that the company violated sanctions imposed on Russia. William Holbrook, a company spokesman, said that the ExxonMobil had followed "clear guidance from the White House and Treasury Department when its representatives signed [in May 2014] documents involving ongoing oil and gas activities in Russia with Rosneft".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(October 2015)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>ExxonMobil is the largest non-government owned company in the energy industry and produces about 3% of the world's oil and about 2% of the world's energy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>ExxonMobil is organized functionally into a number of global operating divisions. These divisions are grouped into three categories for reference purposes, though the company also has several ancillary divisions, such as Coal &amp; Minerals, which are stand alone. It also owns hundreds of smaller subsidiaries such as <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Oil" title="Imperial Oil">Imperial Oil Limited</a> (69.6% ownership) in Canada, and <a href="/wiki/SeaRiver_Maritime" title="SeaRiver Maritime">SeaRiver Maritime</a>, a petroleum shipping company.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Upstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Upstream (petroleum industry)">Upstream</a> (oil exploration, extraction, shipping, and wholesale operations) based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Downstream_(petroleum_industry)" title="Downstream (petroleum industry)">Downstream</a> (marketing, refining, and retail operations) based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a></li>
<li>Chemical division based in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, Texas</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upstream">Upstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Upstream">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The upstream division makes up the majority of ExxonMobil's revenue, accounting for approximately 70% of the total.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  In 2014, the company had 25.3 billion barrels (4.02<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>9</sup> m<sup>3</sup>) of oil-equivalent reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters230215_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters230215-103">[103]</a></sup>  In 2013, its reserves replacement ratio was 103%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters230215_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters230215-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, ExxonMobil's petroleum exploration and production activities are concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakken_Formation" title="Bakken Formation">Bakken Formation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodford_Shale" title="Woodford Shale">Woodford Shale</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caney_Shale" title="Caney Shale">Caney Shale</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>. In addition, ExxonMobil has several gas developments in the regions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcellus_Shale" title="Marcellus Shale">Marcellus Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utica_Shale" title="Utica Shale">Utica Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haynesville_Shale" title="Haynesville Shale">Haynesville Shale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Shale" title="Barnett Shale">Barnett Shale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville_Shale" title="Fayetteville Shale">Fayetteville Shale</a>. All natural gas activities are conducted by its subsidiary, XTO Energy.  As of December 31, 2014, ExxonMobil owned 14.6 million acres (59,000 km<sup>2</sup>) in the United States, of which 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>) were offshore, 1.5 million acres (6,100 km<sup>2</sup>) of which were in the Gulf of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-104">[104]</a></sup>  In California, it has a joint venture called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aera_Energy_LLC" title="Aera Energy LLC">Aera Energy LLC</a> with <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">Shell Oil</a>. In Canada, the company holds 5.4 million acres (22,000 km<sup>2</sup>), including 1 million acres (4,000 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore and 0.7 million acres (2,800 km<sup>2</sup>) of the <a href="/wiki/Kearl_Oil_Sands_Project" title="Kearl Oil Sands Project">Kearl Oil Sands Project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Argentina, ExxonMobil holds 0.9 million acres (3,600 km<sup>2</sup>), Germany 4.9 million acres (20,000 km<sup>2</sup>), in the Netherlands ExxonMobil owns 1.5 million acres (6,100 km<sup>2</sup>), in Norway it owns 0.4 million acres (1,600 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, and the United Kingdom 0.6 million acres (2,400 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore. In Africa, upstream operations are concentrated in Angola where it owns 0.4 million acres (1,600 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, Chad where it owns 46,000 acres (19,000 ha), Equatorial Guinea where it owns 0.1 million acres (400 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore, and Nigeria where it owns 0.8 million acres (3,200 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-104">[104]</a></sup>  In addition, Exxon Mobil plans to start exploration activities off the coast of Liberia and the Ivory Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters131115_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters131115-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters171214_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters171214-106">[106]</a></sup>  In the past, ExxonMobil had exploration activities in Madagascar, however these operations were ended due to unsatisfactory results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters040715_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters040715-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Asia, it holds 9,000 acres (3,600 ha) in Azerbaijan, 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>) in Indonesia, of which 1.3 million acres (5,300 km<sup>2</sup>) are offshore, 0.7 million acres (2,800 km<sup>2</sup>) in Iraq, 0.3 million acres (1,200 km<sup>2</sup>) in Kazakhstan, 0.2 million acres (810 km<sup>2</sup>) in Malaysia, 65,000 acres (26,000 ha) in Qatar, 10,000 acres (4,000 ha) in Yemen, 21,000 acres (8,500 ha) in Thailand, and 81,000 acres (33,000 ha) in the United Arab Emirates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_104-3"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Russia, ExxonMobil holds 85,000 acres (34,000 ha) in the <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a> project. Together with <a href="/wiki/Rosneft" title="Rosneft">Rosneft</a>, it has developed 63.6 million acres (257,000 km<sup>2</sup>) in Russia, including the <a href="/wiki/East-Prinovozemelsky_field" title="East-Prinovozemelsky field">East-Prinovozemelsky field</a>. In Australia, ExxonMobil held 1.7 million acres (6,900 km<sup>2</sup>), including 1.6 million acres (6,500 km<sup>2</sup>) offshore. It also operates the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Longford_Gas_Conditioning_Plant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Longford Gas Conditioning Plant (page does not exist)">Longford Gas Conditioning Plant</a>, and participates in the development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gorgon_LNG" title="Gorgon LNG">Gorgon LNG</a> project. In Papua New Guinea, it holds 1.1 million acres (4,500 km<sup>2</sup>), including the <a href="/wiki/PNG_Gas" title="PNG Gas">PNG Gas</a> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters-XOM_104-4"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-XOM-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downstream">Downstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Downstream">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil markets products around the world under the brands of <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">Mobil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Esso" title="Esso">Esso</a>. Mobil is ExxonMobil's primary retail gasoline brand in California, Florida, New York, New England, the Great Lakes and the Midwest. Exxon is the primary brand in the rest of the United States, with the highest concentration of retail outlets located in New Jersey, Pennsylvania, Texas and in the Mid-Atlantic and Southeastern states. Esso is ExxonMobil's primary gasoline brand worldwide except in Australia and New Zealand, where the Mobil brand is used exclusively. In Colombia, both the Esso and Mobil brands are used.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In Japan, ExxonMobil has a 22% stake in TonenGeneral Sekiyu K.K., a refining company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>&gt;
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemicals">Chemicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Chemicals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil Chemical is a petrochemical company which was created by merging Exxon's and Mobil's chemical industries.  Its principal products includes basic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olefin" title="Olefin">olefins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aromatic" title="Aromatic">aromatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethylene_glycol" title="Ethylene glycol">ethylene glycol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene" title="Polyethylene">polyethylene</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polypropylene" title="Polypropylene">polypropylene</a> along with speciality lines such as <a href="/wiki/Elastomer" title="Elastomer">elastomers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plasticizer" title="Plasticizer">plasticizers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">solvents</a>, process fluids, <a href="/wiki/Oxo_alcohol" title="Oxo alcohol">oxo alcohols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adhesive" title="Adhesive">adhesive</a> <a href="/wiki/Resin" title="Resin">resins</a>. The company also produces synthetic lubricant base stocks as well as lubricant additives, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Propylene" title="Propylene">propylene</a> packaging films and <a href="/wiki/Catalysis" title="Catalysis">catalysts</a>. The company was an industry leader in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metallocene_catalyst" title="Metallocene catalyst">metallocene catalyst</a> technology to make unique polymers with improved performance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ExxonMobil is the largest producer of butyl rubber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>Infineum, a joint venture with Royal Dutch Shell, is manufacturing and marketing <a href="/wiki/Crankcase" title="Crankcase">crankcase</a> lubricant additives, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel_additive" title="Fuel additive">fuel additives</a>, and specialty lubricant additives, as well as <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission_fluid" title="Automatic transmission fluid">automatic transmission fluids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gear_oil" title="Gear oil">gear oils</a>, and industrial oils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clean_technology_research">Clean technology research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Clean technology research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>ExxonMobil conducts research on clean energy technologies, including <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Algael_fuel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Algael fuel (page does not exist)">algae biofuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> made from agricultural waste, carbonate <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cells</a>, and refining crude oil into plastic by using a <a href="/wiki/Membrane" title="Membrane">membrane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osmosis" title="Osmosis">osmosis</a> instead of heat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg031117_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg031117-112">[112]</a></sup>  However, it is unlikely the company will commercialize these projects before 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bloomberg031117_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg031117-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_data">Financial data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Financial data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(January 2016)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 2005, ExxonMobil surpassed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> as the world's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publicly_held_corporation" title="Publicly held corporation">publicly held corporation</a> when measured by revenue, although Wal-Mart remained the largest by number of employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006dethrone_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-2006dethrone-113">[113]</a></sup>  ExxonMobil's $340 billion revenues in 2005 were a 25.5 percent increase over their 2004 revenues.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 2006, Wal-Mart recaptured the lead with revenues of $348.7 billion against ExxonMobil's $335.1. ExxonMobil continued to lead the world in both profits ($39.5 billion in 2006) and market value ($460.43 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2006WalMart_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-2006WalMart-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, ExxonMobil had a record net income of $40.61 billion on $404.552 billion of revenue, an increase largely due to escalating oil prices as their actual BOE production decreased by 1 percent, in part due to expropriation of their <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan</a> assets by the <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Hugo Chávez">Chávez</a> government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of December 2013, ExxonMobil occupied five out of ten slots for <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_corporate_profits_and_losses" title="List of largest corporate profits and losses">Largest Corporate Annual Earnings of All Time</a> and two out of ten on <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_corporate_profits_and_losses" title="List of largest corporate profits and losses">Largest Corporate Quarterly Earnings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG/220px-ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG/330px-ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG/440px-ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobilDowntownHoustonTX.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_Building" title="ExxonMobil Building">ExxonMobil Building</a>, former ExxonMobil offices in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">Downtown Houston</a> were vacated in early 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>ExxonMobil's headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> As of May 2015, the company was nearing completion of its new campus located in a northern <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Spring,_Texas" title="Spring, Texas">Spring</a>, at the intersection of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_45" title="Interstate 45">Interstate 45</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hardy_Toll_Road" title="Hardy Toll Road">Hardy Toll Road</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Parkway" title="Grand Parkway">Grand Parkway</a> northern extension. It is an elaborate corporate campus, including twenty office buildings totaling 3,000,000 square feet (280,000 m<sup>2</sup>), a wellness center, laboratory, and three parking garages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> It is designed to house nearly 10,000 employees with an additional 1,500 employees located in a satellite campus in Hughes Landing in <a href="/wiki/The_Woodlands,_Texas" title="The Woodlands, Texas">The Woodlands, Texas</a>. In October 2010, the company stated that it would not move its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">Greater Houston</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The current chairman of the board and CEO of Exxon Mobil Corp. is Darren W. Woods. Woods was elected chairman of the board and CEO effective January 1, 2017 after the retirement of former chairman and CEO Rex Tillerson. Before his election as chairman and CEO, Woods was elected president of ExxonMobil and a member of the board of directors in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exxon-Mobil-Corporation-Dec-2016-8-K_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exxon-Mobil-Corporation-Dec-2016-8-K-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  January 11, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the current ExxonMobil board members are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoardofDirector_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-BoardofDirector-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Boskin" title="Michael Boskin">Michael Boskin</a>, professor of economics <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, director of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corp.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shinsei_Bank" title="Shinsei Bank">Shinsei Bank</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vodafone_Group" title="Vodafone Group">Vodafone Group</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Brabeck-Letmathe" title="Peter Brabeck-Letmathe">Peter Brabeck-Letmathe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> chairman and former Nestlé CEO</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Angela_F._Braly&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Angela F. Braly (page does not exist)">Angela F. Braly</a>, former CEO of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WellPoint" title="WellPoint">WellPoint</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ursula_Burns" title="Ursula Burns">Ursula Burns</a>, Xerox chairman and CEO</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Larry_R._Faulkner" title="Larry R. Faulkner">Larry R. Faulkner</a>, president, Houston Endowment; president emeritus, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henrietta_H._Fore" title="Henrietta H. Fore">Henrietta H. Fore</a>, Holsman International</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Frazier" title="Kenneth Frazier">Kenneth Frazier</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">Merck &amp; Co.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Douglas_R._Oberhelman" title="Douglas R. Oberhelman">Douglas R. Oberhelman</a>, chairman and chief executive officer, <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar Inc.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Palmisano" title="Samuel J. Palmisano">Samuel J. Palmisano</a>, chairman of the board, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IBM_Corporation" title="IBM Corporation">IBM Corp.</a></li>
<li>Steven S Reinemund, retired executive chairman of the board, <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_C._Weldon" title="William C. Weldon">William C. Weldon</a>, past <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a> chairman</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darren_W._Woods" title="Darren W. Woods">Darren W. Woods</a>, chairman of the board and CEO, ExxonMobil Corporation</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
