<p>ExxonMobil's environmental record has been a target of critics from outside organizations such as the environmental lobby group <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> as well as some public employee pension funds that disagree with its stance on global warming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Political_Economy_Research_Institute" title="Political Economy Research Institute">Political Economy Research Institute</a> ranks ExxonMobil sixth among corporations emitting <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Air pollution in the United States">airborne pollutants in the United States</a>. The ranking is based on the quantity (15.5 million pounds in 2005) and toxicity of the emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2005, ExxonMobil had committed less than 1 percent of their profits towards researching alternative energy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> less than other leading oil companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Funding_of_global_warming_disinformation_and_denial"></span>
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil_climate_change_controversy" title="ExxonMobil climate change controversy">ExxonMobil climate change controversy</a></div>
<p>ExxonMobil's activities related to climate change has varied over the decades. From the late 1970s through the 1980s, Exxon funded research broadly in line with the developing public scientific approach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes20151009_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes20151009-127">[127]</a></sup> After the 1980s, Exxon curtailed its own climate research and was a leader in <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">climate change denial</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icn20150921_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-icn20150921-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20070209_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20070209-130">[130]</a></sup> In 2014, ExxonMobil publicly acknowledged climate change risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>  It nominally supports a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tax" title="Carbon tax">carbon tax</a>, though that support is weak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icn311215_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-icn311215-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>ExxonMobil funded organizations opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> and seeking to influence public opinion about the scientific consensus that <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> is caused by the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian20070209_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20070209-130">[130]</a></sup> ExxonMobil helped to found and lead the <a href="/wiki/Global_Climate_Coalition" title="Global Climate Coalition">Global Climate Coalition</a>, which opposed greenhouse gas emission regulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icn20150921_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-icn20150921-128">[128]</a></sup> In 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Concerned_Scientists" title="Union of Concerned Scientists">Union of Concerned Scientists</a> said that ExxonMobil granted $16 million, between 1998 and 2005, towards 43 advocacy organizations which dispute the impact of global warming, and that ExxonMobil used disinformation tactics similar to those used by the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_industry" title="Tobacco industry">tobacco industry</a> in its denials of the link between lung cancer and smoking, saying that the company used many of the same organizations and personnel to cloud the scientific understanding of climate change and delay action on the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ucs200702_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-ucs200702-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of  March 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the attorneys general of New York, California, Massachusetts, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> are investigating, with the cooperation of 17 US states, whether ExxonMobil misled consumers or investors regarding the risks of climate change. Exxon said the investigations were "politically motivated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sakhalin-I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin-I" title="Sakhalin-I">Sakhalin-I</a></div>
<p>Scientists and environmental groups have voiced concern that the Sakhalin-I oil and gas project in the Russian Far East, operated by an ExxonMobil subsidiary Exxon Neftegas, threatens the critically endangered western <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whale</a> population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwf240409_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwf240409-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>  Particular concerns were caused by the decision to construct a pier and to start shipping in Piltun Lagoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ens110716_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-ens110716-139">[139]</a></sup> ExxonMobil has responded that since 1997 the company has invested over $40 million to the western whale monitoring program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phys040916_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-phys040916-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jersey_settlement">New Jersey settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: New Jersey settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil-New_Jersey_environmental_contamination_settlement" title="ExxonMobil-New Jersey environmental contamination settlement">ExxonMobil-New Jersey environmental contamination settlement</a></div>
<p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Department_of_Environmental_Protection" title="New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection">New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection</a> sued ExxonMobil for $8.9 billion for lost wetland resources at <a href="/wiki/Constable_Hook" title="Constable Hook">Constable Hook</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bayonne,_New_Jersey" title="Bayonne, New Jersey">Bayonne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayway_Refinery" title="Bayway Refinery">Bayway Refinery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Linden,_New_Jersey" title="Linden, New Jersey">Linden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NJDEP_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-NJDEP-141">[141]</a></sup> Although a <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court" title="New Jersey Superior Court">New Jersey Superior Court</a> justice was believed to be close to a ruling, the <a href="/wiki/Governorship_of_Chris_Christie" title="Governorship of Chris Christie">Christie Administration</a> repeatedly asked the judge to wait, since they were reaching a settlement with ExxonMobil's attorneys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-142">[142]</a></sup>  On Friday, February 19th, 2015, lawyers for the Christie administration informed the judge that a deal had been reached. Details of the $225 million settlement - roughly 3% of what the state originally sought - were not immediately released. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Porrino" title="Christopher Porrino">Christopher Porrino</a> served as Chief Counsel to the <a href="/wiki/Governorship_of_Chris_Christie" title="Governorship of Chris Christie">Christie administration</a> from January 2014 through July 2015 and handled negotiations in the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT030515_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT030515-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Accusations_of_ExxonMobil_human_rights_violations_in_Indonesia" title="Accusations of ExxonMobil human rights violations in Indonesia">Accusations of ExxonMobil human rights violations in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>ExxonMobil is the target of human rights activists for actions taken by the corporation in the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> territory of <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>. In June 2001, a lawsuit against ExxonMobil was filed in the Federal <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">District Court</a> of <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">the District of Columbia</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alien_Tort_Claims_Act" title="Alien Tort Claims Act">Alien Tort Claims Act</a>. The suit alleges that the ExxonMobil knowingly assisted human rights violations, including <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>, murder and rape, by employing and providing material support to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Indonesia" title="Military of Indonesia">Indonesian military</a> forces, who committed the alleged offenses during <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">civil unrest</a> in Aceh. Human rights complaints involving Exxon's (Exxon and Mobil had not yet merged) relationship with the Indonesian military first arose in 1992; the company denies these accusations and filed a <a href="/wiki/Motion_(legal)" title="Motion (legal)">motion to dismiss</a> the suit, which was denied in 2008 by a federal judge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> But another federal judge dismissed the lawsuit in August 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The plaintiffs are currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> appealing the dismissal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> ExxonMobil was  ranked as the 12th best of 92 oil, gas, and mining companies on indigenous rights in its Arctic operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geopolitical_influence">Geopolitical influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Geopolitical influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A July 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">Daily Telegraph</a></i> review of <a href="/wiki/Steve_Coll" title="Steve Coll">Steve Coll</a>'s book, <i>Private Empire: ExxonMobil and American Power</i>, says that he thinks that ExxonMobil is "able to determine American foreign policy and the fate of entire nations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tel12_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-15">[15]</a></sup> ExxonMobil increasingly drills in terrains leased to them by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dictatorships" title="Dictatorships">dictatorships</a>, such as those in <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tel12_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-15">[15]</a></sup> Steve Coll describes <a href="/wiki/Lee_Raymond" title="Lee Raymond">Lee Raymond</a>, the corporation's chief executive until 2005, as "notoriously skeptical about climate change and disliked government interference at any level".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tel12_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-tel12-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The book was also reviewed in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, according to which "ExxonMobil is easy to caricature, and many critics have done so.... It is to Steve Coll's credit that <i>Private Empire</i>, his new book about ExxonMobil, refuses to subscribe to such a simplistic view."  The review describes the company's power in dealing with the countries in which it drills as "constrained".  It notes that the company shut down its operations in Indonesia to distance itself from the abuses committed against the population by that country's army, and that it decided to drill in Chad only after the World Bank agreed to ensure that the oil royalties were used for the population's benefit.  The review closes by noting that "A world addicted to ExxonMobil's product needs to look in the mirror before being too critical of how relentlessly the company supplies it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">Accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Exxon Valdez oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a></div>
<p>The March 24, 1989, <a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez_oil_spill" title="Exxon Valdez oil spill">Exxon Valdez oil spill</a> resulted in the discharge of approximately 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil into <a href="/wiki/Prince_William_Sound" title="Prince William Sound">Prince William Sound</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-149">[149]</a></sup> oiling 1,300 miles (2,100 km) of the remote Alaskan coastline. The Valdez spill is 36th worst <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spill</a> in history in terms of sheer volume.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The State of Alaska's Exxon Valdez Oil Spill Trustee Council stated that the spill "is widely considered the number one spill worldwide in terms of damage to the environment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-149">[149]</a></sup> Carcasses were found of over 35,000 birds and 1,000 sea otters. Because carcasses typically sink to the seafloor, it is estimated the death toll may be 250,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seabirds" title="Seabirds">seabirds</a>, 2,800 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_otters" title="Sea otters">sea otters</a>, 300 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbor_seals" title="Harbor seals">harbor seals</a>, 250 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bald_eagles" title="Bald eagles">bald eagles</a>, and up to 22 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Killer_whales" title="Killer whales">killer whales</a>. Billions of <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herring#Life_cycle" title="Herring">herring eggs</a> were also killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2001, oil remained on or under more than half the sound's beaches, according to a 2001 federal survey. The government-created Exxon Valdez Oil Spill Trustee Council concluded that the oil disappears at less than 4 percent per year, adding that the oil will "take decades and possibly centuries to disappear entirely". Of the 27 species monitored by the council, 17 have not recovered. While the salmon population has rebounded, and the orca whales are recovering, the herring population and fishing industry have not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>Exxon was widely criticized for its slow response to cleaning up the disaster. John Devens, the Mayor of Valdez, has said his community felt betrayed by Exxon's inadequate response to the crisis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Exxon later removed the name "Exxon" from its tanker shipping subsidiary, which it renamed "<a href="/wiki/SeaRiver_Maritime" title="SeaRiver Maritime">SeaRiver Maritime</a>". The renamed subsidiary, though wholly Exxon-controlled, has a separate corporate charter and board of directors, and the former <i><a href="/wiki/Exxon_Valdez" title="Exxon Valdez">Exxon Valdez</a></i> is now the <i>SeaRiver Mediterranean</i>. The renamed tanker is legally owned by a small, stand-alone company, which would have minimal ability to pay out on claims in the event of a further accident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>After a trial, a jury ordered Exxon to pay $5 billion in punitive damages, though an appeals court reduced that amount by half. Exxon appealed further, and on June 25, 2008, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a> lowered the amount to $500 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supreme_appeal_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-supreme_appeal-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Exxon still uses more single-hull tankers than the rest of the largest ten oil companies combined, including the Valdez's sister ship, the SeaRiver Long Beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nightingale_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nightingale-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Exxon.27s_Brooklyn_oil_spill"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Exxon's_Brooklyn_oil_spill">Exxon's Brooklyn oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Exxon's Brooklyn oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenpoint_oil_spill" title="Greenpoint oil spill">Greenpoint oil spill</a></div>
<p>New York Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> announced on July 17, 2007 that he had filed suit against the Exxon Mobil Corp. and ExxonMobil Refining and Supply Co. to force cleanup of the oil spill at Greenpoint, Brooklyn, and to restore <a href="/wiki/Newtown_Creek" title="Newtown Creek">Newtown Creek</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cuomo_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-cuomo-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study of the spill released by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="US Environmental Protection Agency">US Environmental Protection Agency</a> in September 2007 reported<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> that the spill consists of 17 to 30 million US gallons (64,000 to 114,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of petroleum products from the mid-19th century to the mid-20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The largest portion of these operations were by ExxonMobil or its predecessors. By comparison, the Exxon Valdez oil spill was approximately 11 million US gallons (42,000 m<sup>3</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EVOSTC_FAQ_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-EVOSTC_FAQ-149">[149]</a></sup>  The study reported that in the early 20th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_New_York" title="Standard Oil of New York">Standard Oil of New York</a> operated a major refinery in the area where the spill is located. The refinery produced fuel oils, gasoline, kerosene and solvents. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naptha" title="Naptha">Naptha</a> and gas oil, secondary products, were also stored in the refinery area. Standard Oil of New York later became Mobil, a predecessor to Exxon/Mobil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baton_Rouge_Refinery_pipeline_oil_spill">Baton Rouge Refinery pipeline oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Baton Rouge Refinery pipeline oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2012, a crude oil pipeline, from the Exxon Corp Baton Rouge Refinery, burst and spilled at least 1,900 barrels of oil (80,000 gallons) in the rivers of Point Coupee Parish, Louisiana, shutting down the Exxon Corp Baton Refinery for a few days. Regulators opened an investigation in response to the pipeline oil spill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters-April-2012_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-April-2012-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baton_Rouge_Refinery_benzene_leak">Baton Rouge Refinery benzene leak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Baton Rouge Refinery benzene leak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 14, 2012, a bleeder plug on a tank in the <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge_Refinery" title="Baton Rouge Refinery">Baton Rouge Refinery</a> failed and began leaking <a href="/wiki/Naphtha" title="Naphtha">naphtha</a>, a substance that is composed of many chemicals including <a href="/wiki/Benzene" title="Benzene">benzene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> ExxonMobil originally reported to the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Department_of_Environmental_Quality" title="Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality">Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality</a> (LDEQ) that 1,364 pounds of material had been leaked.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>On June 18, Baton Rouge refinery representatives told the LDEQ that ExxonMobil's chemical team determined that the June 14 spill was actually a level 2 incident classification which means that a significant response to the leak was required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-164">[164]</a></sup> On the day of the spill the refinery did not report that their estimate of spilled materials was significantly different from what was originally reported to the department. Because the spill estimate and the actual amount of chemicals spilled varied drastically, the LDEQ launched an in-depth investigation on June 16 to determine the actual amounts of chemicals spilled as well as to find out what information the refinery knew and when they knew it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-165">[165]</a></sup>   On June 20, ExxonMobil sent an official notification to the LDEQ saying that the leak had actually released 28,688 pounds of benzene, 10,882 pounds of toluene, 1,100 pounds of cyclohexane, 1,564 pounds of hexane and 12,605 pounds of additional volatile organic compound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-165">[165]</a></sup> After the spill, people living in neighboring communities reported adverse health impacts such as severe headaches and respiratory difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="621" data-file-width="2853" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg/600px-ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg/900px-ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg/1200px-ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ExxonMobil_Baton_Rouge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ExxonMobil refinery in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">Baton Rouge</a></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yellowstone_River_oil_spill">Yellowstone River oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Yellowstone River oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="967" data-file-width="1066" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg/200px-YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg/300px-YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg/400px-YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YellowstoneRiverMap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Yellowstone River watershed</div></div></div>
<p>The July 2011 Yellowstone River oil spill was an oil spill from an ExxonMobil pipeline running from Silver Tip to <a href="/wiki/Billings,_Montana" title="Billings, Montana">Billings, Montana</a>, which ruptured about 10 miles west of Billings on July 1, 2011, at about 11:30 pm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-July-11_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-July-11-167">[167]</a></sup> The resulting spill leaked an estimated 1,500 barrels of oil into the <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_River" title="Yellowstone River">Yellowstone River</a> for about 30 minutes before it was shut down, resulting in about $135 million in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pipelines_and_Hazardous_Materials_Safety_Administration_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pipelines_and_Hazardous_Materials_Safety_Administration-168">[168]</a></sup> As a precaution against a possible explosion, officials in <a href="/wiki/Laurel,_Montana" title="Laurel, Montana">Laurel, Montana</a> evacuated about 140 people on Saturday (July 2) just after midnight, then allowed them to return at 4 am.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-July-11_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-July-11-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>A spokesman for ExxonMobil said that the oil is within 10 miles of the spill site. However, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Montana" title="List of Governors of Montana">Montana Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Schweitzer" title="Brian Schweitzer">Brian Schweitzer</a> disputed the accuracy of that figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The governor pledged that "The parties responsible will restore the Yellowstone River."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HS3-jul-11_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-HS3-jul-11-170">[170]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayflower_oil_spill">Mayflower oil spill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Mayflower oil spill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2013_Mayflower_oil_spill" title="2013 Mayflower oil spill">2013 Mayflower oil spill</a></div>
<p>On March 29, 2013, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pegasus_Pipeline&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pegasus Pipeline (page does not exist)">Pegasus Pipeline</a>, owned by ExxonMobil and carrying Canadian <a href="/wiki/Wabasca_oil_field" title="Wabasca oil field">Wabasca</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_sands" title="Oil sands">heavy crude</a>, ruptured in <a href="/wiki/Mayflower,_Arkansas" title="Mayflower, Arkansas">Mayflower, Arkansas</a>, releasing about 3,190 barrels (507 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil and forcing the evacuation of 22 homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters120815_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120815-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The Environmental Protection Agency has classified the leak as a <i>major spill</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>  In 2015, ExxonMobil settled charges that it violated the federal Clean Water Act and state environmental laws, for $5.07 million, including $4.19 million in civil penalties. It did not admit liability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters120815_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters120815-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=ExxonMobil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Yergin" title="Daniel Yergin">Yergin, Daniel</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prize:_The_Epic_Quest_for_Oil,_Money,_and_Power" title="The Prize: The Epic Quest for Oil, Money, and Power">The Prize: The Epic Quest for Oil, Money, and Power</a></i>. New York: <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Schuster" title="Simon &amp; Schuster">Simon &amp; Schuster</a>, 1991.</li></ul>
</div>
